The evolution of deposition morphology was explored by further increasing the capacity (Supplementary Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#MOESM2">30</a>), WCIE showed Na adaptation at high capacity. The dynamic sodium plating process was monitored by optical microscopy to illustrate the morphological evolution. As the preferred nucleation site for sodium deposition, the SMA surfaces of Base and LF electrolytes ranged from numerous spikes appearing at 5 min of deposition to being covered with flocculated sodium dendrites at 20 min (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#Fig4">4</a>d1, d2, Supplementary Videos&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#MOESM7">4</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#MOESM8">5</a>). In contrast, the SMA of WCIE showed a smooth and dense morphology without dendrites throughout the plating process (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#Fig4">4</a>d3, Supplementary Video&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#MOESM1">6</a>). In addition, the mechanical stability of the SEI for WCIE is higher than the Base and LF electrolytes, this is consistent with the atomic force microscope (AFM) (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#Fig4">4</a>e1-e3). Therefore, the compact SEI formed by WCI solvation structure are dense, and the presence of abundant grain boundaries for the inorganic components allows efficient Na<sup>+</sup> migration, which is not hindered by the internal structure of SEI, achieving rapid and uniform deposition<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 31" title="Wu, Y. et al. Electrostatic potential as solvent descriptor to enable rational electrolyte design for lithium batteries. Adv. Energy Mater. 13, 2300259 (2023)." href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#ref-CR31" id="ref-link-section-d4923709e1381">31</a></sup>. In addition, cyclic voltammetry (CV), exchange current density and Temperature-dependent electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (EIS) showed the benefits of WCIE in electrochemical kinetics (Supplementary Figs.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#MOESM2">31</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#MOESM2">32</a>, tables&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#MOESM2">3</a>–<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#MOESM2">5</a>, and Note&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#MOESM2">8</a>). The battery capacity loss was further quantified to investigate the dissolution of SEI by the electrolyte in real cases (See Supplementary Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#MOESM2">33</a> and Note&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#MOESM2">9</a> for specific details)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 5" title="Jin, Y. et al. Low-solvation electrolytes for high-voltage sodium-ion batteries. Nat. Energy 7, 718–725 (2022)." href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#ref-CR5" id="ref-link-section-d4923709e1408">5</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 48" title="Ma, L. A., Naylor, A. J., Nyholm, L. &amp; Younesi, R. Strategies for mitigating dissolution of solid electrolyte interphases in sodium-ion batteries. Interface Angew. Chem. Int. Ed. 60, 4855–4863 (2021)." href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#ref-CR48" id="ref-link-section-d4923709e1411">48</a></sup>. The capacity growth after each pause indicates that the anode electrolyte decomposition produces a parasitic reduction reaction to compensate for the dissolution of the SEI formed during the long open circuit pause (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#Fig4">4f</a>). The capacity loss after a xh long pause (the difference between capacity after and before the pause) quantifies SEI dissolution in the electrolyte (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#Fig4">4g</a>). The average capacity loss of Base electrolyte after 50 h pause (5.82 µAh) was 1.1 times for LF electrolyte (5.38 µAh) and 3.3 times for WCIE (1.77 µAh). Notably, the actual dissolution of SEI is much more severe on the inhomogeneous anode surface exposed with porous after cycling. In addition, the dissolution of SEI in LF electrolyte remains slow and persistent, with an average capacity loss after the last 5 h pause (0.773 µAh) that is 1.9 times for WCIE (0.403 µAh). The dissolution of SEI was largely suppressed in WCIE, as evidenced by the lowest capacity loss, the least variable SEI fraction, and the most stable long-cycle performance (Supplementary Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#MOESM2">34</a> and Note&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#MOESM2">9</a>). This highlights the strengths of WCIE: a solvation structure with less active free solvent, low polarity DFBn and more salt decomposition derived SEI with lower solubility, further demonstrating the contribution of beneficial solvation structure to stable SEI even a good anode, paving the way for subsequent electrochemical performance.</p><div class="c-article-section__figure js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="figure" data-container-section="figure" id="figure-4" data-title="Characterization of Na plating/stripping morphology."><figure><figcaption><b id="Fig4" class="c-article-section__figure-caption" data-test="figure-caption-text">Fig. 4: Characterization of Na plating/stripping morphology.</b></figcaption><div class="c-article-section__figure-content"><div class="c-article-section__figure-item"><a class="c-article-section__figure-link" data-test="img-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="image" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w/figures/4" rel="nofollow"><picture><source type="image/webp" srcset="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41467-024-50751-w/MediaObjects/41467_2024_50751_Fig4_HTML.png?as=webp"><img aria-describedby="Fig4" src="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41467-024-50751-w/MediaObjects/41467_2024_50751_Fig4_HTML.png" alt="figure 4" loading="lazy" width="685" height="711"></picture></a></div><div class="c-article-section__figure-description" data-test="bottom-caption" id="figure-4-desc"><p>Top and Side-view SEM images of Cu foils in (<b>a1</b>, <b>a2</b>) Base, (<b>b1</b>, <b>b2</b>) LF and (<b>c1</b>, <b>c2</b>) WCIE cycled for 100 cycles at 1 mA cm<sup>−2</sup> and 1 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup>. In situ optical microscopy images showing cross-sections of symmetric cells at (<b>d1</b>) Base, (<b>d2</b>) LF, and (<b>d3</b>) WCIE plating Na electrodes. AFM surface and 3D topography analysis of Na electrodeposits on Cu foils in (<b>e1</b>) Base, (<b>e2</b>) LF and (<b>e3</b>) WCIE at 1 mA cm<sup>−2</sup> and 1 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup>. <b>f</b> Capacity from electrolyte reduction reactions (at 1 µA cm<sup>−2</sup>) before and after each pause as a function of the number of cycles. <b>g</b> Capacity loss of three parallel cells with different pause times in different electrolytes.</p></div></div><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="article-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="button" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w/figures/4" data-track-dest="link:Figure4 Full size image" aria-label="Full size image figure 4" rel="nofollow"><span>Full size image</span><svg width="16" height="16" focusable="false" role="img" aria-hidden="true" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#icon-eds-i-chevron-right-small"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec6">Compatibility with sodium anodes</h3><p>After analyzing the effects of different electrolyte solvation structures on the structural composition, deposition morphology and kinetics of the SEI, the electrochemical reversibility of Na metal was assessed by various electrochemical performances. For the Na | |Cu cells (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#Fig5">5a, b</a> and Supplementary Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#MOESM2">35</a>), the reversibility of CE was about 86.5% and 91% with low cycle life at 1 mA cm<sup>−2</sup> and 1 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup> in Base and LF electrolytes. The SEI produced by the action of solvation clusters in both electrolytes were fragile and poorly tolerant to high currents<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 49" title="Zhou, P. et al. Rationally designed fluorinated amide additive enables the stable operation of lithium metal batteries by regulating the interfacial chemistry. Nano Lett. 22, 5936–5943 (2022)." href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#ref-CR49" id="ref-link-section-d4923709e1522">49</a></sup>. Surprisingly, WCIE-formed SEI achieved stable Na<sup>+</sup> plating/stripping over 600 cycles with an average CE of 97.5% and a low voltage hysteresis (224 mV). The CE values derived from the Aurbach<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 50" title="Adams, B. D., Zheng, J., Ren, X., Xu, W. &amp; Zhang, J.-G. Accurate determination of coulombic efficiency for lithium metal anodes and lithium metal batteries. Adv. Energy Mater. 8, 1702097 (2018)." href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#ref-CR50" id="ref-link-section-d4923709e1529">50</a></sup> method also indicate the advantages of the WCIE (Supplementary Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#MOESM2">36</a> and Note&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#MOESM2">10</a>). Fixed capacity CE measurements were performed at different current densities to examine the adaptability of Na plating/stripping (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#Fig5">5c, d</a> and Supplementary Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#MOESM2">37</a>). Maintaining a capacity of 1 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup>, the CE of Base and LF electrolytes changed dramatically when the current density was increased from 0.5 mA cm<sup>−2</sup> – 3 mA cm<sup>−2</sup>. In contrast, WCIE showed good current suitability, returning to 0.5 mA cm<sup>−2</sup> still cycling stably for 600 cycles, along with a low overpotential at high current densities. The low nucleation and growth overpotentials of Na deposition for the first cycle discharge curve at different current densities (Supplementary Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#MOESM2">38</a>) reveal the WCIE imparts highly reversible Na plating/stripping<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 51" title="Pei, A., Zheng, G., Shi, F., Li, Y. &amp; Cui, Y. Nanoscale nucleation and growth of electrodeposited lithium metal. Nano Lett. 17, 1132–1139 (2017)." href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#ref-CR51" id="ref-link-section-d4923709e1557">51</a></sup>. Summarizing recent studies on Na | |Cu cells (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#Fig5">5e</a>, Supplementary table&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#MOESM2">6</a>), the results show useful progress in our work, demonstrating the beneficial effects of the solvation structure and SEI of WCIE compared to conventional ester electrolytes. Na | |Na cells were further evaluated for long-term plating/stripping stability of sodium metal (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#Fig5">5f</a>). Operating at 1 mA cm<sup>−2</sup> and 1 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup> for &lt;1500 h, Base and LF electrolyte rapidly failed due to dendrite formation and continued electrolyte depletion. Impressively, WCIE exhibited low voltage hysteresis and regular voltage distribution for up to 2500 h. The low <i>R</i><sub><i>int</i></sub> from EIS curves (Supplementary Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#MOESM2">39</a>) also suggests that SEI is well suited for Na<sup>+</sup> migration. In addition, after changing the capacity to 2 mA cm<sup>−2</sup>–4 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup>, 5 mA cm<sup>−2</sup>–1 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup>, and rate (Supplementary Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#MOESM2">40</a>), the WCIE still have the capability of cycling for &gt;1000 h, 350 h, and a stable rate cycling ability, respectively. Na | |Na cells also show better performance than most ester electrolytes (Supplementary Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#MOESM2">41</a>, Supplementary table&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#MOESM2">7</a>) in the literature. The above cell performance results further indicate that WCI solvation clusters greatly improve the cycling stability of sodium metal in phosphate ester electrolytes.</p><div class="c-article-section__figure js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="figure" data-container-section="figure" id="figure-5" data-title="Electrochemical performances testing of Na | |Cu and Na | |Na cells."><figure><figcaption><b id="Fig5" class="c-article-section__figure-caption" data-test="figure-caption-text">Fig. 5: Electrochemical performances testing of Na | |Cu and Na | |Na cells.</b></figcaption><div class="c-article-section__figure-content"><div class="c-article-section__figure-item"><a class="c-article-section__figure-link" data-test="img-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="image" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w/figures/5" rel="nofollow"><picture><source type="image/webp" srcset="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41467-024-50751-w/MediaObjects/41467_2024_50751_Fig5_HTML.png?as=webp"><img aria-describedby="Fig5" src="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41467-024-50751-w/MediaObjects/41467_2024_50751_Fig5_HTML.png" alt="figure 5" loading="lazy" width="685" height="574"></picture></a></div><div class="c-article-section__figure-description" data-test="bottom-caption" id="figure-5-desc"><p><b>a</b> CE test in Na | |Cu cells using different electrolytes at 1 mA cm<sup>−2</sup> and 1 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup>. <b>b</b> Capacity-Voltage curves for corresponding WCIE. <b>c</b> Fixed 1 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup> capacity, Na | |Cu cells CE test at different current densities. <b>d</b> Na plating/stripping voltage hysteresis corresponding to different electrolytes. <b>e</b> Comparison of CE between recently reported work and the present work. <b>f</b> Voltage profiles of Na | |Na symmetric cells in different electrolytes at 1 mA cm<sup>−2</sup> and 1 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup>.</p></div></div><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="article-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="button" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w/figures/5" data-track-dest="link:Figure5 Full size image" aria-label="Full size image figure 5" rel="nofollow"><span>Full size image</span><svg width="16" height="16" focusable="false" role="img" aria-hidden="true" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#icon-eds-i-chevron-right-small"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec7">High-Voltage Na | |PB cells testing and cathodic passivation</h3><p>From the DFT and PDOS results, the solvation clusters have high HOMO values, and the oxidation of Base and LF electrolyte solvation clusters dominates the cathodic passivation reaction, with the HOMO of the preferentially oxidized conduction bands being located on EMC and TMP, resulting in the formation of organic, inhomogeneous CEI<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 27" title="Zhang, J. et al. Weakly solvating cyclic ether electrolyte for high-voltage lithium metal batteries. ACS Energy Lett. 8, 1752–1761 (2023)." href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#ref-CR27" id="ref-link-section-d4923709e1661">27</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 38" title="Li, Z. et al. Non-polar ether-based electrolyte solutions for stable high-voltage non-aqueous lithium metal batteries. Nat. Commun. 14, 868 (2023)." href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#ref-CR38" id="ref-link-section-d4923709e1664">38</a></sup>. WCI solvation clusters formed by WCIE likewise have high HOMO values. On the contrary, the HOMO of the preferentially oxidized conduction bands of WCI solvation clusters are located on TFSI<sup>−</sup>, favoring the formation of inorganic CEI to cathodic passivation. As we predicted, WCIE showed beneficial cycling stability at high-voltage 4.7 V (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#Fig6">6a</a>). The capacity of cells with Base and LF electrolytes decayed rapidly during cycling, and CE was chaotic. Although EMC was replaced with TMP to increase the oxidation voltage of LF electrolyte to about 5.0 V in the LSV, the full cells still showed poor stability during cycling. One, due to the catalytic effect of PB cathode, the LF electrolyte started to decompose far below the tested oxidation voltage in the actual full cells. The second is due to the formation of solvent-rich clusters leading to the formation of brittle SEI/CEI at 4.7 V for long cycles<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 52" title="Bai, P. et al. Formation of LiF-rich cathode-electrolyte interphase by electrolyte reduction. Angew. Chem. Int. Ed. 61, e202202731 (2022)." href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#ref-CR52" id="ref-link-section-d4923709e1673">52</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 53" title="Rinkel, B. L. D., Vivek, J. P., Garcia-Araez, N. &amp; Grey, C. P. Two electrolyte decomposition pathways at nickel-rich cathode surfaces in lithium-ion batteries. Energy Environ. Sci. 15, 3416–3438 (2022)." href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#ref-CR53" id="ref-link-section-d4923709e1676">53</a></sup>. The capacity retention after 200 cycles was 84.3% and the average CE was 99.5% for WCIE. Corresponding capacity-voltage curves (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#Fig6">6b</a> and Supplementary Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#MOESM2">42</a>) also show low overpotential. Rate performance showed that WCIE could discharge at a higher rate (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#Fig6">6c</a>). The discharge capacity of WCIE was still 118.7 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> and 105.1 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 10 C and 20 C, respectively, with high CE and narrow voltage gap (Supplementary Figs.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#MOESM2">43</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#MOESM2">44</a>). EIS investigated the charge transfer kinetics of different electrolytes after cycling (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#Fig6">6d</a>). The low CEI and charge transfer impedance of WCIE suggests beneficial CEI and a low Na<sup>+</sup> embedding/detachment impedance at the electrode<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 54" title="Kim, S. C. et al. High-entropy electrolytes for practical lithium metal batteries. Nat. Energy 8, 814–826 (2023)." href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#ref-CR54" id="ref-link-section-d4923709e1706">54</a></sup>. Self-discharge tests were performed to further probe the high-voltage resistance of different electrolytes (Supplementary Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#MOESM2">45</a> and Note&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#MOESM2">11</a>). In addition, WCIE has much less parasitic reactions to the cathode at high voltage, inhibiting side reactions and Al corrosion (Supplementary Figs.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#MOESM2">46</a>–<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#MOESM2">49</a> and Note&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#MOESM2">12</a>). WCIE also has some promising applications in hard carbon anodes and sodium ion batteries. (Supplementary Figs.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#MOESM2">50</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#MOESM2">51</a> and Note&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#MOESM2">13</a>).</p><div class="c-article-section__figure js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="figure" data-container-section="figure" id="figure-6" data-title="Electrochemical performances testing and cathode characterization of Na | |PB cells."><figure><figcaption><b id="Fig6" class="c-article-section__figure-caption" data-test="figure-caption-text">Fig. 6: Electrochemical performances testing and cathode characterization of Na | |PB cells.</b></figcaption><div class="c-article-section__figure-content"><div class="c-article-section__figure-item"><a class="c-article-section__figure-link" data-test="img-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="image" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w/figures/6" rel="nofollow"><picture><source type="image/webp" srcset="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41467-024-50751-w/MediaObjects/41467_2024_50751_Fig6_HTML.png?as=webp"><img aria-describedby="Fig6" src="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41467-024-50751-w/MediaObjects/41467_2024_50751_Fig6_HTML.png" alt="figure 6" loading="lazy" width="685" height="600"></picture></a></div><div class="c-article-section__figure-description" data-test="bottom-caption" id="figure-6-desc"><p><b>a</b> Long-term cycling of different electrolytes at 4.7 V (PB loading: ~3 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup>). <b>b</b> Capacity-Voltage curves for corresponding WCIE. <b>c</b> Rate performances of different electrolytes at 4.7 V. <b>d</b> EIS curves for different electrolytes at 4.7 V after 50 cycles. <b>e1</b>, <b>f1</b> Base, (<b>e2</b>, <b>f2</b>) LF, (<b>e3</b>, <b>f3</b>) WCIE of PB cathode at 4.7 V after 80 cycles SEM and HRTEM. XPS analysis (<b>g</b>) and Corresponding atomic concentration contents (<b>h</b>) of PB cathode after 80 cycles.</p></div></div><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="article-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="button" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w/figures/6" data-track-dest="link:Figure6 Full size image" aria-label="Full size image figure 6" rel="nofollow"><span>Full size image</span><svg width="16" height="16" focusable="false" role="img" aria-hidden="true" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#icon-eds-i-chevron-right-small"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><p>We observed morphology of electrode material and CEI after cycling in different systems using SEM and high-resolution transmission electron microscopy (HRTEM) (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#Fig6">6e, f</a>). In the Base electrolyte, particles on the electrode surface were severely agglomerated and formed a thick and inhomogeneous CEI. This is due to a series of complex chain reactions such as oxidative decomposition of electrolyte on high-voltage, corrosion of Al collector, and dissolution of transition metals<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 52" title="Bai, P. et al. Formation of LiF-rich cathode-electrolyte interphase by electrolyte reduction. Angew. Chem. Int. Ed. 61, e202202731 (2022)." href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#ref-CR52" id="ref-link-section-d4923709e1800">52</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 53" title="Rinkel, B. L. D., Vivek, J. P., Garcia-Araez, N. &amp; Grey, C. P. Two electrolyte decomposition pathways at nickel-rich cathode surfaces in lithium-ion batteries. Energy Environ. Sci. 15, 3416–3438 (2022)." href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#ref-CR53" id="ref-link-section-d4923709e1803">53</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 55" title="Li, S. et al. Synergistic dual-additive electrolyte enables practical lithium-metal batteries. Angew. Chem. Int. Ed. 59, 14935–14941 (2020)." href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#ref-CR55" id="ref-link-section-d4923709e1806">55</a></sup>. Despite the improvement of LF electrolyte, it still does not achieve good protection. The material has a smooth surface with well-defined edges, forming a thin and uniform CEI (7 nm) in WCIE. Stable and homogeneous CEI is closely related to the structural composition, the chemical composition of CEI was investigated using XPS (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#Fig6">6g</a>). In F 1 <i>s</i> spectra, the major peaks correspond to NaF and C-F, respectively. 160.2 eV in the S 2<i>p</i> spectra corresponds to Na<sub>2</sub>S, and 397.3 eV in the N 1 <i>s</i> spectra is Na<sub>3</sub>N. NaF, Na<sub>2</sub>S and Na<sub>3</sub>N are the main inorganic components that are very effective in the construction of thin and homogeneous CEI, are decomposition products of TFSI<sup>−</sup> and FEC, inhibit electrode/electrolyte side-reactions and facilitate Na<sup>+</sup> transport<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Luo, C. et al. Synergistic-effect of diluent to reinforce anion-solvation-derived interfacial chemisty for 4.5 V-class Li||LiCoO2 batteries. Nano Energy 109, 108323 (2023)." href="#ref-CR25" id="ref-link-section-d4923709e1836">25</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Yoo, D. J., Yang, S., Kim, K. J. &amp; Choi, J. W. Fluorinated aromatic diluent for high-performance lithium metal batteries. Angew. Chem. Int. Ed. 59, 14869–14876 (2020)." href="#ref-CR26" id="ref-link-section-d4923709e1836_1">26</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 27" title="Zhang, J. et al. Weakly solvating cyclic ether electrolyte for high-voltage lithium metal batteries. ACS Energy Lett. 8, 1752–1761 (2023)." href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#ref-CR27" id="ref-link-section-d4923709e1839">27</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 33" title="Xu, J. et al. Electrolyte design for Li-ion batteries under extreme operating conditions. Nature 614, 694–700 (2023)." href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#ref-CR33" id="ref-link-section-d4923709e1842">33</a></sup>. The same C = O, C-O and S-O peaks are present in O 1 <i>s</i> spectra. However, the peaks at 530.3 eV for Base and LF electrolytes are attributed to M-O (M = Fe, Mn, etc.), showing significant dissolution of transition metals and the formation of CEI that have broken down and become inhomogeneous<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 56" title="Hu, P. et al. Concentration-gradient prussian blue cathodes for Na-ion batteries. ACS Energy Lett. 5, 100–108 (2019)." href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#ref-CR56" id="ref-link-section-d4923709e1849">56</a></sup>. Organic products such as RONa and ROCONa accumulated on cathode surface are mainly decomposition products of electrolyte. In C 1 <i>s</i> spectra, the strongest peak at 284.8 eV corresponds to C-C/C-H, which is mainly related to conductive agent<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 26" title="Yoo, D. J., Yang, S., Kim, K. J. &amp; Choi, J. W. Fluorinated aromatic diluent for high-performance lithium metal batteries. Angew. Chem. Int. Ed. 59, 14869–14876 (2020)." href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#ref-CR26" id="ref-link-section-d4923709e1856">26</a></sup>. The elemental contents of different CEI were compared by quantitative XPS analysis (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#Fig6">6h</a>). WCIE had low C, O and P contents and high inorganic F, N and S contents. Therefore, the NaF/Na<sub>3</sub>N/Na<sub>2</sub>S-rich CEI layer was denser and more homogeneous, the smaller thickness and beneficial composition ensured rapid Na<sup>+</sup> migration across CEI. These results indicate that WCI solvation clusters formed by WCIE not only provide a robust CEI, but also inhibit solvent oxidation and Al collector corrosion, improving the stability of full cells during charge/discharge<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 37" title="Lee, S. H. et al. Toward the sustainable lithium metal batteries with a new electrolyte solvation chemistry. Adv. Energy Mater. 10, 2000567 (2020)." href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#ref-CR37" id="ref-link-section-d4923709e1870">37</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 57" title="Fan, X. et al. Non-flammable electrolyte enables Li-metal batteries with aggressive cathode chemistries. Nat. Nanotechnol. 13, 715–722 (2018)." href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#ref-CR57" id="ref-link-section-d4923709e1873">57</a></sup>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec8">Special and practical conditions for NallPB cells</h3><p>Finally, the electrochemical performance of three electrolytes was investigated in various SMBs. NallPB cells performance was firstly investigated at 60 °C with a highly loaded PB cathode (3 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup>) (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#Fig7">7a, b</a> and Supplementary Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#MOESM2">52</a>). Base and LF electrolytes fail equally quickly, with WCIE showing significantly better cycling stability at high temperature, with 85% capacity retention after 200 cycles and an average CE of 99.5%. As a result, WCIE also show high temperature application possibilities, with the advantage of solvation minimizing unfavorable overcharging. In addition, considering wide temperature application ranges of phosphate and DFBn, the electrochemical performance of Na | |PB cells was tested from −30 °C to 70 °C at 4.7 V (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#Fig7">7c</a>). At 30 °C, the discharge capacity of WCIE is close to LF electrolyte. However, the difference in capacity begins to appear when the temperature is lowered to 10 °C. When the temperature dropped to −30 °C, WCIE still had a capacity of 110.6 mA h g<sup>−1</sup>, Base electrolyte appeared to be in disarray and LF electrolyte was left with only 72.5 mA h g<sup>−1</sup>. Capacity-voltage curves further proved the advantages of WCIE at different temperatures (Supplementary Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#MOESM2">53</a>). To investigate WCIE at a higher voltage, we tested Na | |PB cells at a cut-off voltage of 4.8 V (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#Fig7">7d, e</a>). Na | |PB cells could not be charged up to 4.8 V due to the coupling between carbonate solvent and TFSI<sup>−</sup> in Base electrolyte and the unfavorable solvation structure leading to easy decomposition under high-voltage (Supplementary Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#MOESM2">54</a>)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 58" title="Chen, Z. et al. Anion solvation reconfiguration enables high-voltage carbonate electrolytes for stable Zn/graphite cells. Angew. Chem. Int. Ed. 59, 21769–21777 (2020)." href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#ref-CR58" id="ref-link-section-d4923709e1912">58</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 59" title="Borodin, O., Behl, W. &amp; Jow, T. R. Oxidative stability and initial decomposition reactions of carbonate, sulfone, and alkyl phosphate-based. Electrolytes J. Phys. Chem. C. 117, 8661–8682 (2013)." href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#ref-CR59" id="ref-link-section-d4923709e1915">59</a></sup>. In contrast, WCIE has beneficial cycling stability and boasts a high-capacity retention after cycling with an average CE of 99.3%. Similarly, Na | |PB cells shows beneficial performance at 20 C (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#Fig7">7f</a> and Supplementary Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#MOESM2">55</a>). Only slight voltage polarization and degradation were observed at an ultra-high charging voltage, suggesting that the solvated layer of the WCIE has good compatibility with SEI/CEI formed at such high voltage. Based on the beneficial electrochemical performance of WCIE at the anode/cathode, a full Na | |PB cells with an N/P ratio of 4:1 was matched and cycled at 4.7 V (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#Fig7">7g, h</a> and Supplementary Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#MOESM2">56</a>) WCIE not only has an average CE of 99.5% and capacity retention of 85% over 150 cycles with a narrow charge/discharge gap, but also has fast kinetic properties with capacities of 98.1 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> and 76.7 Ah g<sup>−1</sup> at rates of 10 C and 20 C, respectively (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#Fig7">7i</a> and Supplementary Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#MOESM2">57</a>). Similarly, stable cycling was achieved with N/P ratio of 2:1 and anode-free condition (Supplementary Figs.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#MOESM2">58</a>–<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#MOESM2">61</a> and Notes&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#MOESM2">14</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w#MOESM2">15</a>). Therefore, our design strategy using WCI has good application prospects.</p><div class="c-article-section__figure js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="figure" data-container-section="figure" id="figure-7" data-title="Electrochemical performances testing of Na | |PB cells under special conditions."><figure><figcaption><b id="Fig7" class="c-article-section__figure-caption" data-test="figure-caption-text">Fig. 7: Electrochemical performances testing of Na | |PB cells under special conditions.</b></figcaption><div src="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41467-024-50751-w/MediaObjects/41467_2024_50751_Fig7_HTML.png" alt="figure 7" loading="lazy" width="685" 3 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup> cathode-load at 4.7 V, 60 °C. <b>b</b> Capacity-Voltage curves for corresponding WCIE. <b>c</b> Electrochemical performances testing using different electrolytes at temperatures from −30 °C–70 °C. <b>d</b> Long-term cycling of different electrolytes at 4.8 V. <b>e</b> Capacity-Voltage curves for corresponding WCIE at 4.8 V. <b>f</b> Rate performances of different electrolytes at 4.8 V. <b>g</b>–<b>i</b> Electrochemical performances testing of Na | |PB full cells with an N/P ratio of 4: 1 at 4.7 V.</p></div></div><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="article-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="button" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41467-024-50751-w/figures/7" data-track-dest="link:Figure7 Full size image" aria-label="Full size image figure 7" rel="nofollow"><span>Full size image</span><svg width="16" height="16" focusable="false" role="img" aria-hidden="true" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#icon-eds-i-chevron-right-small"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div></div></div></section><section data-title="Discussion"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec9-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec9">Discussion</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec9-content"><p>In conclusion, we have reconfigured the solvation behavior of phosphate-based electrolytes by exploiting intermolecular interactions to improve the performance and the compatibility of SMBs. Our WCIE system is shown to extend the operation of SMBs at high-voltage, which exceeds the currently reported cell performances by feasible cells configurations (Na<span class="stix">‖</span>Cu cells, Na<span class="stix">‖</span>Na cells, variable temperature high-load cathode, and controlled N/P ratio). The relative LUMO and HOMO of the solvated clusters are modulated due to the weakly coordinating-intervention of Na<sup>+</sup> by DFBn and the solvation behavior enriched with Na<sup>+</sup>, which directs the decomposition sequence of electrolyte on the anode/cathode surface to form a strong anion-dominated interfacial layer. More importantly, this work not only proposes an effective theoretical design principle to overcome the poor stability of electrolytes for SMBs, but also elucidates the correlation between the solvation structure and the redox behavior of electrolyte, SEI dissolution, and anodic/cathodic protection. Meanwhile, it is determined that the SEI/CEI chemical changes in SMBs are due to differences in solvation rather than differences in the mechanism of SEI formation, which is a useful advance for SMBs. The design and beneficial performance of WCIE provide a reliable approach to the study of existing SMAs in Na plating/stripping reversibility, long-term operation of high-voltage SMBs. Our results also provide an insight into understanding the process of interface formation and tailoring its chemical composition.</p></div></div></section><section data-title="Methods"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec10-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec10">Methods</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec10-content"><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec11">Materials</h3><p>Sodium metal was obtained from Alfa Aesar Reagent Co. (99.9%) (Supplier: Shanghai Mern Chemical Technology Co.). The salts, solvents, including Sodium trifluoromethanesulfonimide (NaTFSI) (battery-grade purity), Ethyl Methyl Carbonate (EMC) (battery-grade purity), Fluoroethylene carbonate (FEC) (battery-grade purity) were purchased from Duoduo Chemical Reagent Co., Ltd. The Trimethyl phosphate (TMP) was purchased from ALFA (Supplier: Shanghai Titan Technology Co.) with purity of &gt;98%. 1,2-difluorobenzene (DFBn) was purchased from TCl (Shanghai) Kasei Industry Development Co., with purity of &gt;98%. Before preparing the electrolyte, the solvent was dried by 4 Å zeolite to ensure that the water content was below 10 ppm. Prussian Blue (PB) cathodes were purchased from Naba Co., Ltd. Chemical reagents. Coin chute (stainless steel, SS-316), collector (aluminum and copper foil with purity of &gt;99%), conductive carbon, and polyvinylidene fluoride (PVDF) were purchased from TOB New Energy Technology Co. Glass fiber separator (GF/C) was purchased from Whatman Company. Copper and aluminum foils (thickness 10 µm, diameter 15 mm) were cleaned of surface dust and impurities with ethanol before use. The copper foil did not have any surface treatment before use. Electrolytes were prepared by mixing the required amount of salt, solvent. The usage of electrolyte in button cell was 90 µL. The preparation of electrolytes was all carried out in a glove box with O<sub>2</sub>, and H<sub>2</sub>O content &lt; 1 ppm.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec12">Material characterization</h3><p>The viscosity was collected on TA Instruments DHR-2 rotational rheometer with accurate temperature control system. The contact angle was collected on the instrument DSA-30 Droplet Shape Analyser. The flammability tests of electrolytes were carried out in the fume hood. The morphological of cycles studies were obtained by HITACHI S-4800 field emission scanning electron microscopy (FESEM) and Bruker Dimension Icon Atomic Force Microscope (AFM). To analyze the chemical composition of SEI and CEI, characterization of electrodes after cycling using XPS measurements (Thermo Scientific ESCALAB Xi<sup>+</sup>, American). It is accompanied with depth profiling, which is performed by Ar<sup>+</sup> sputtering. High resolution transmission electron microscope (HRTEM) images were obtained from a TECNAI F30 at 300 kV. The cycled cells were disassembled in the glove box filled with argon (the contents of O<sub>2</sub> and H<sub>2</sub>O were kept below 0.1 ppm) and the electrodes were washed with dimethyl ether (DME) before morphology and composition characterizations. The in-situ dynamic Na deposition behaviors were observed at 0.5 mA cm<sup>−2</sup> for 30 min by ZOOM-0850C (SHANGHAI PUQIAN OPTICAL INSTRUMENT CO., LTD.) using Na as working electrode. Raman results were captured on XploRA with an excitation laser wavelength of 532 nm. <sup>13</sup>C NMR spectra were recorded at room temperature (295 K) with a Bruker Avance III HD 850 MHz spectrometer. For NMR measurements, 600 µL of electrolyte sample was placed in the outer tube of a 5 mm NMR Wilmad coaxial tube.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec13">Electrochemical measurements</h3><p>The ionic conductivities (<i>σ</i>) and Electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (EIS) of different electrolytes were tested by electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (IM6, Zahner Elektrik, Germany) tests of button cells in a frequency range from 0.1 Hz – 10<sup>5 </sup>Hz with an amplitude voltage of 5 mV. The electrodes were assembled with two stainless steels (SS | | SS). The ionic conductivity (<i>σ</i><sub><i>Na</i></sub>) was calculated using the following equation:</p><div id="Equ1" class="c-article-equation"><div class="c-article-equation__content"><span class="mathjax-tex">$${\sigma }_{{Na}}=\frac{L}{R\times S}$$</span></div><div class="c-article-equation__number">
                    (1)
                </div></div><p>Where <i>R</i> is the bulk resistance, <i>L</i> is the thickness of the membrane, <i>S</i> is the contact area of inert electrode (stainless steel). In this work, the thickness of membrane is 0.13 mm, and the diameter is 19 mm.</p><p>The Na<sup>+</sup> transference number (<i>t</i><sub><i>Na+</i></sub>) of different electrolytes were measured by DC polarization (POL) combined with EIS tests of Na | | Na symmetrical coin cells on Zaher and calculated from the following equation:</p><div id="Equ2" class="c-article-equation"><div class="c-article-equation__content"><span class="mathjax-tex">$${t}_{{Na}+}=\frac{{I}_{s}\times {R}_{1}^{s}(\Delta V-{I}_{0}\times {R}_{2}^{0})}{{I}_{0}\times {R}_{1}^{0}(\Delta V-{I}_{s}\times {R}_{2}^{s})}$$</span></div><div class="c-article-equation__number">
                    (2)
                </div></div><p>where <i>ΔV</i> is the POL voltage (10 mV), <i>I</i><sub><i>0</i></sub> and <i>I</i><sub><i>s</i></sub> are the response current at the initial and after stabilization, respectively. <i>R</i><sub><i>1</i></sub><sup><i>0</i></sup> and <i>R</i><sub><i>2</i></sub><sup><i>0</i></sup> are the bulk ohmic resistance and interfacial charge transfer resistance of the Na | |Na cells before POL, respectively. <i>R</i><sub><i>1</i></sub><sup><i>s</i></sup> and <i>R</i><sub><i>2</i></sub><sup><i>s</i></sup> are the bulk ohmic resistance and interfacial charge transfer resistance of the Na | |Na cells after stabilization.</p><p>Sodium metal anodes were obtained after extruding sodium metal foil (~1 mm) into discs (Ф 14.0, ≥99.9%) using a stainless-steel punch with a diameter of 14.0 mm. Prior to preparation, white oxide powder was removed from the surface using scissors to obtain sodium with a silvery-white metallic luster. Afterwards, the lumps of sodium metal were pressed into sodium foils with a thickness of about 1 mm using a roller press, and then pressed into sodium anodes with a diameter of 14 mm using a punch. To prevent deterioration of the sodium metal due to excessive storage in the glove box, it is cut and used now before assembling the battery. The oxygen and water content of the glove box was &lt;1 ppm and the ambient temperature was 25 °C during the whole operation. Electrochemical cycling and rate tests were assembled by 2032-type coin batteries with glass fiber (Whatman GF-C) and tested by using a battery test system (Shenzhen NEWARE Co. LTD, China). The Na | |Cu cells were using Cu foil as working electrode, Na metal disk as counter electrode. The coulombic efficiency (CE) of the Na | |Cu cells was calculated by charge/discharge capacity, and the stripping cut-off potential was set to 1 V. Na | |Na symmetric cells were assembled by using two piece of Na disks as working and counter electrodes. Stainless steel (SS-316) discs and springs were added to the Na piece to ensure even pressure distribution. The battery was allowed to stand for 6 h before testing to allow the electrodes and membrane to wet completely. EIS in frequency ranges from 0.1 Hz – 10<sup>5 </sup>Hz with amplitude of 5 mV and we used Zview software to fit the temperature-dependent EIS. To perform the impedance test at different temperatures, the cells were first set aside for 2 h at different temperatures. Cyclic voltammetry (CV, Squidstat prime) tests within potential range of −0.3–3 V vs. Na/Na<sup>+</sup> at scan rate of 1 mV s<sup>−1</sup>. The oxidation potential of the electrolytes was tested by linear sweep voltammetry (LSV, Squidstat prime) of Na | |SS cells. The chronoamperometry (CA) measurements was tested by Squidstat prime. The charge/discharge performance of electrolytes were obtained by assembled full cells using PB as cathode, Na metal as anode and a piece of GF-C as separator in an Ar-filled glove box (glove box with O<sub>2</sub> and H<sub>2</sub>O content &lt;1 ppm). Prussian blue electrodes were prepared by mixing Prussian blue powder, conductive carbon, and PVDF binder in N Methyl-2-Pyrrolidone (NMP) in the ratio of 80:10:10 by weight to form a homogeneous paste. Round electrodes of 13 mm diameter were then cut, pressed, dried in a vacuum oven at 120 °C for a further 12 h and weighed. Cycle and rate tests were performed on the NEWARE battery test system at 25 °C. All Na | |PB cells were tested in a voltage range between 2.4 – 4.5 V, 2.4 – 4.7 V or 2.4 – 4.8 V vs. Na/Na<sup>+</sup>. All full cells were activated for 2 cycles at 0.2 C. The PB loading was around 3 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup> for both cycling and rate tests for Na | |PB cells with cut-off voltages of 4.5 V and 4.7 V. The PB loading was around 5 mg cm<sup>−2</sup> for both cycling and rate tests for Na | |PB cells with cut-off voltages of 4.8 V. Low-temperature and change-temperature full cells test was performed by connect with NEWARE battery test system. The electrochemical performance and EIS at different temperatures was carried out within an RTP-80CT high and low temperature test chamber (Guangdong Huan Rui Test Equipment Co., Ltd, China). All cells were maintained at specified temperature for 2 h prior to testing. Final specific capacity was determined to the active mass of PB. The Na | |PB full cells were fabricated with negative/positive capacity (N/P) ratio of 4 (For the N/P negative electrode fabrication, 6 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup> of sodium metal was deposited onto the smooth copper foil to form a composite electrode and the areal capacity of cathode is 1.5 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup>). The Na | |PB cells contains practical loading of anode (3 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup>) and PB cathode (1.5 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup>) in N/P ratio = 2. The Na | |PB cells contains practical loading of PB cathode (3 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup>) in N/P ratio = 0.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec14">Computational details</h3><p>Ab initio Molecular Dynamics (AIMD) simulations were performed using the Vienna Ab initio Simulation Package (VASP 5.4) based on the pseudopotential plane-wave approach. The Perdew-Burke-Ernzerhof generalized gradient approximation (GGA-PBE) was utilized to represent the exchange-correlation functional, with a cutoff energy of 400 eV. The initial configurations of NaTFSI, FEC, EMC, TMP, TTE, FBn and DFBn were optimized using Gaussian09 program with M062X/6-311 + G (d, p). The NaTFSI salt/solvent mixtures (base, LF, LHCEs, FBn-based electrolyte and WCIE) were prepared by randomly placing the molecules in the simulation box based on their experimental densities and molar ratios. A cubic-shaped simulation box of length 1.357 nm was used for all dimensions. We performed DFT relaxation to equilibrate the structure after randomly packing the box. Then AIMD simulations were performed at 300 K using the NVT ensemble with a time step of 1.0 fs. Temperature oscillations were controlled using a Nose thermostat with a Nose-mass parameter of 1.0. A Monkhorst-Pack k-point mesh grid scheme with a 1 × 1 × 1 grid was used. The systems were equilibrated for at least 60 ps before the production run of 10 ps. The projected density of states (PDOS) was calculated and averaged over five different configurations (extracted from AIMD simulation snapshots) to represent an ensemble average. The HOMO, LUMO energy levels of salt/solvent molecules were directly calculated and optimized by a basis set of B3LYP/6-311 G + + (d, p). The HOMO and LUMO energy levels for solvation complex were calculated using the B3LYP/6-31 G (d, p) basis set for structure optimization, while the single point energies were calculated using the larger B3LYP/6-311 G + + (d, p) basis set. Radial distribution functions were obtained by the Visual Molecular Dynamics (VMD) software. The VESTA program was used to sample the most probable solvation shells from the simulation trajectory. In addition, ESPs of molecules were calculated with Gaussian09 program at the B3LYP/def2tzvp level and visualized by GaussView.</p></div></div></section>
                    
                </div>

C.W. designed the experiments and analyzed the results. C.W., Z.S., Y.L., L.L., J.F., and R.Y. analyzed and interpreted the experimental data. X.Y. and J.Y. carried out AFM measurements. R.Y. performed the theoretical calculations. Q.H. performed the Raman experiments. C.W. and Z.S. drafted the paper with support from M.Z. and Q.D. All authors discussed the results and commented on the manuscript. The work was supervised by M.Z. and Q.D.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="corresponding-author">Corresponding authors</h3><p id="corresponding-author-list">Correspondence to
